    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

<span id="freeTextContainer8652198265498639126">It has been four months since a mysterious obsidian stone fell into Kell's possession. Four months since his path crossed with Delilah Bard. Four months since Prince Rhy was wounded, and since the nefarious Dane twins of White London fell, and four months since the stone was cast with Holland's dying body through the rift--back into Black London.<br/><br/>Now, restless after having </span>
  <span id="freeText8652198265498639126" style="display:none">It has been four months since a mysterious obsidian stone fell into Kell's possession. Four months since his path crossed with Delilah Bard. Four months since Prince Rhy was wounded, and since the nefarious Dane twins of White London fell, and four months since the stone was cast with Holland's dying body through the rift--back into Black London.<br /><br />Now, restless after having given up his smuggling habit, Kell is visited by dreams of ominous magical events, waking only to think of Lila, who disappeared from the docks as she always meant to do. As Red London finalizes preparations for the Element Games--an extravagant international competition of magic meant to entertain and keep healthy the ties between neighboring countries--a certain pirate ship draws closer, carrying old friends back into port.<br /><br />And while Red London is caught up in the pageantry and thrills of the Games, another London is coming back to life. After all, a shadow that was gone in the night will reappear in the morning. But the balance of magic is ever perilous, and for one city to flourish, another London must fall.</span>

        if (this.up('#box')) {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: $('box').getStyle('z-index')})});

        $('edition_29939337').observe('prototip:shown', function () {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function (e) {
            if ($('edition_29939337').hasClassName('ignored')) {
              e.setStyle({'display': 'none'});

<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_392541'><a id="like_count_community_question_392541" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/392541?resource_type=CommunityQuestion"><span class="likesCount">3 likes</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F20764879-a-gathering-of-shadows">like</a></span>

<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/1695365-victoria-schwab"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1442505907i/1695365._UX100_CR0,16,100,100_.jpg" /></a>

<span class='communityAnswererName'>

</span>

          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: 6000})});
        }
      });
      $('span_class_gr-hyperlink_sort_order_span_tip_391').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

//]]>
</script>    </div>

<div id="review_1845324375" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1845324375" />
    <a title="Petrik" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/59458347-petrik"><img alt="Petrik" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1568016775p2/59458347.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1845324375?book_show_action=true">May 28, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Petrik" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Petrik" href="/user/show/59458347-petrik">Petrik</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781783295425" href="/book/show/26236443-a-gathering-of-shadows">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1845324375" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13266024629229807315"><b>It’s unbelievable how I started this book with the lowest possible expectation and it still managed to disappoint me.</b> I know this is a beloved book in the YA community, you might wanna stay away from reading this review if you’re easily offended. Seriously stay away.<br/><br/>I think it’s better for me to start off with the parts I like about the book first, there’s only a few anyway. First, Holland, every single appearance from him made the plot and the book so much better, despite his appearance being r</span>
  <span id="freeText13266024629229807315" style="display:none"><b>It’s unbelievable how I started this book with the lowest possible expectation and it still managed to disappoint me.</b> I know this is a beloved book in the YA community, you might wanna stay away from reading this review if you’re easily offended. Seriously stay away.<br><br>I think it’s better for me to start off with the parts I like about the book first, there’s only a few anyway. First, Holland, every single appearance from him made the plot and the book so much better, despite his appearance being rarer than the amount of Hinduism in my city. Second, the last 50 pages of the book were actually quite good, with some flaws but at least it’s captivating. Finally, VE Schwab's prose remained great to read as always. Holland is literally the only character that pushed me into finishing this trilogy cause I need to know more about him and his fate.<br><br>Now, for all the shit, A Gathering of Shadows, where do I even begin with the problem in this one? Let’s start with an easy one first. This book is majorly afflicted with the infamous 2nd book syndrome, the first 350 pages are painful to read, pretty much a pointless filler. A cow’s opinion is better than these 350 pages and for god sake a cow’s dialogue is literally only “moo” “moo” “moo”, see how pointless that sounds? Well, that’s how the first 350 pages are. It’s about preparing for a magical arena tournament, which ended up being a huge copycat of Avatar: The Legend of Korra.<br><br>The battles in the arena itself are okay at best which made reading the 350 pages of nothing completely a worthless experience. Don't get me wrong, I love slow paced books, most adult fantasy books I read are slow paced and trust me, the books I love used these pages carefully. Building character developments, slowly building relationship, explain more on the world-building aspect etc. Not spending time brooding, doing insta-love, random making out and obsessing over Delilah fucking Bard, which I’ll get into in a moment.<br><br>I’m also very disappointed with how much time the characters spent on Red London, seriously there are 4 London, make use of them please. What’s the point of creating 4 London if the story is going to take place almost all the time in Red London?? What are you doing? Trying to make us see the color of apple in London? Every time the story shifted to White London <i>(scarcely)</i> it’s actually so much better. However, the most significant problem I had with the book lies in one and one factor only. The damn characters, especially Lila fucking Bard or Lila fucking bad or Lila fucking Bald, whatever her special damned kind is.<br><br>Kell and Rhy spent all their time here fighting and whining over being saved? <b>“WAHHH WAHHHHH YOU SAVED MEEEEE LET ME DIEEEEE BUT I WANNA LIVE AND I’M SAD WAHHH WAHHH YOU PISSED ME OFF”</b><br><br>Dude….. kill yourself… bite your tongue, chop your head off, climb the Big Ben like you belong in the Assassin Creed and jump yourself to death, I don’t care just… stop whining over being saved. Seriously I can’t stress this enough, other than Holland I seriously just want all these characters to die. BUT none of them can compare to the ultimate Mary Sue, Delilah fucking bard, the Wonder Woman, the alien, the predator, whatever she is cause she doesn’t know too.<br><br>I was led to believe the main character of this series is Kell, I was wrong. It was Lila, the narrative treated the reader as if we’re brain damaged or have short term memory. It will remind us countless times during everyone’s POV that Lila is unlike most girls. I liked her in the first book and I can’t believe how much I hated her in this installment. She’s an ultimate Mary Sue, apparently 4 months is enough to become a fluent speaker in a new language, and become a magician, from a thief. In the first book she was just a thief. In this one she’s a female Voldemort but wait… I shouldn’t call her a female because she’s one of a damned kind.<br><br>Here's most dialogues around Lila in the book, featuring me<br><br>Me: Hi Lila<br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“I am one of a damned kind”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br>Me: urmm okay? So how are yo--<br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“I am not most girls.”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br>Me: ….<br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“I am not most girls.”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b> <br>Me: Okay I get it you’re not most girl, you just said—<br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“I am one of a damned kind”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br>Me: Okay you fucking E.T I get--<br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“I am not most girls.” </blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br>Me: Hey-<br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“I am not most girls.”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br>Kell walking towards me with his endless angst and frown but then, seems like a random thought appeared in his head and he said:<br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“Lila is unlike most girls.”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br>Me: STTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTTAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAA- <br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“I am not most girls.”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br>Me: HHHHHHHHHPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPPP!!!<br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“I am one of a damned kind”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1495997037ra/22873540.gif" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Drew Barrymore from the movie ‘50 First Dates’ would’ve remember Delilah fucking Bard for the endless repetition in the narrative to always remind the reader that she’s one of a kind, badass, can do shit, put Lila in a Star Wars and she’ll be the ultimate Jedi oh my lord.<br><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“She bent most of the rules. She broke the rest.”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br>Yeah, including my brain for reading your stupidity.<br><br>Here’s one of the few trying so hard to be badass but idiotic dialogue.<br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“Everyone’s immortal until they’re not.”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br>No shit. What’s next? Everyone’s dead when they’re killed? Everyone’s alive when they have a heartbeat? You can clap if you have hands?<br><br>This is a book that should’ve been condensed by at least 300 pages and it would’ve been so much better. There’s way too many useless information that wouldn’t affect anything in the main story. Plus the ending left us in a cliffhanger just when the story FINALLY about to get interesting and now I have to continue because my momma didn’t raise a quitter and I’m not about to quit now. I’ve prepared some alcohol for my next read, I hope it could be better but my expectation for the last book is minus zero.<br><br>If you enjoy the book, I'm truly happy for you. I wish I could but I can't.. not for this one. Also, if you’re wondering why I’m reading this series, it’s because VE Schwab tricked me completely into thinking that this will be an adult oriented book like her ‘Vicious’ (which I love) and IT’S NOT! If I knew what I’m getting into, I wouldn't had spend any money I worked hard for into this trilogy.<br><br><i>You can find the rest of my Adult Epic/High Fantasy &amp; Sci-Fi reviews at <a href="http://booknest.eu/review/patrick" rel="nofollow noopener">BookNest</a></i></span>
  <a data-text-id="13266024629229807315" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1272774225" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1272774225" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1272774225?book_show_action=true">May 05, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2016">2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=arc">arc</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1272774225" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14385189325364482283"><blockquote>
  <i>Delilah Bard had a way of finding trouble.</i>
</blockquote><br/><b>I just love everything about this world</b>. Read it in a single day and I cannot wait for the next book.<br/><br/>I think I'm a bit of an unintentionally picky reader when it comes to fantasy. A lot of YA fantasy is heavy on the romance and low on the substance, which irks me, but I don't take much pleasure in overlong, dense, wordy adult fantasy series either. I want exciting world-building, strong characters and good pacing that doesn't sacrifice depth. And I f</span>
  <span id="freeText14385189325364482283" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>Delilah Bard had a way of finding trouble.</i>
</blockquote><br /><b>I just love everything about this world</b>. Read it in a single day and I cannot wait for the next book.<br /><br />I think I'm a bit of an unintentionally picky reader when it comes to fantasy. A lot of YA fantasy is heavy on the romance and low on the substance, which irks me, but I don't take much pleasure in overlong, dense, wordy adult fantasy series either. I want exciting world-building, strong characters and good pacing that doesn't sacrifice depth. And I feel like Schwab totally gets that.<br /><br />The writing style is <b>detailed and evocative</b> - you can picture this world so easily, even though it is highly sensational, and you can feel the magic running through it. Schwab crafts scenes with both description and tension, firmly cementing her as one of my favourite fantasy authors.<br /><br />It is a world for those who <b>admire imagination</b>. Alternate Londons, some with magic and some without, magic wielders, evil rulers, pirates and - in this installment - a magical tournament called the Essen Tasch. The author uses this tournament to draw the characters together, to create action and excitement, whilst behind it all there looms a dark threat.<br /><br />With <b>rich, evocative storytelling</b>, an <b>original, fantastically-conceived fantasy world</b>, and <b>colourful, weird characters</b>, it's hard to complain. The book buzzes with magical secrets and new discoveries; like an adult version of Narnia, it is a way of walking through the wardrobe and facing all the wonderful and horrifying possibilities.<br /><br />I enjoyed Kell's new experiences, as he comes to term with the lasting effects of what happened in the last book. I enjoyed all the backstabbing, cross-dressing and thievery. But, most of all, <b>I just freaking love Lila</b>. She is the baddest badass of them all and she doesn't give a shit.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20764879.A_Gathering_of_Shadows__Shades_of_Magic___2_" title="A Gathering of Shadows (Shades of Magic, #2) by V.E. Schwab" rel="nofollow noopener">A Gathering of Shadows</a> goes deeper, drawing us further into this world and developing all the characters. It ends with a promise of more horror and action in the next book. I can't wait.<br /><blockquote>
  <i>After all, you can kill people, but you cannot kill magic.<br />Not truly.</i>
</blockquote><br /><a href="http://thebookgeek.org" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/EmilyMayTheBookGeek" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="https://society6.com/bookgeek/" rel="nofollow noopener">Store</a></span>

<div id="review_2395542368" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2395542368" />
    <a title="Miranda Reads" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/71848701-miranda-reads"><img alt="Miranda Reads" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1592243041p2/71848701.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2395542368?book_show_action=true">Jan 31, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Miranda Reads" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Miranda Reads" href="/user/show/71848701-miranda-reads">Miranda Reads</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/71848701-miranda-reads?shelf=ya-series">ya-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/71848701-miranda-reads?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2395542368" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10097532758395602100"><blockquote>
<img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1605968391i/30408429._SX540_.jpg' width='400' height='225' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Seven of my favorite Bookish Villains in one <b><u><a href='https://youtu.be/sAaQkvGPGag' rel='nofollow noopener'>BookTube Video</a></u></b>!</blockquote><b>
  <u>The Written Review</u>
</b><blockquote>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1567353783i/28084571._SY540_.jpg' width='400' height='400' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
  <br/>
  <br/>
  <i>She bent most of the rules. She broke the rest.</i>
</blockquote><b>There are four Londons, </b>layered on top of each other, each existing without knowing of the other.<br/><br/><b>Black London </b>- wild, untamed magic. All-consuming madness.<br/><b>White London</b> - crippled, desperate, hungry magic. Slowly dying.<br/><b>Red London</b> - vibrant, thriving, full of magic<br/><b>Grey London </b>- the "boring" London, no magic, no spark, no nothing.<br/><br/>Each world is sealed though </span>
  <span id="freeText10097532758395602100" style="display:none"><blockquote>
<img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1605968391i/30408429._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="225" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Seven of my favorite Bookish Villains in one <b><u><a href="https://youtu.be/sAaQkvGPGag" rel="nofollow noopener">BookTube Video</a></u></b>!</blockquote><b>
  <u>The Written Review</u>
</b><blockquote>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1567353783i/28084571._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  <br>
  <br>
  <i>She bent most of the rules. She broke the rest.</i>
</blockquote><b>There are four Londons, </b>layered on top of each other, each existing without knowing of the other.<br><br><b>Black London </b>- wild, untamed magic. All-consuming madness.<br><b>White London</b> - crippled, desperate, hungry magic. Slowly dying.<br><b>Red London</b> - vibrant, thriving, full of magic<br><b>Grey London </b>- the "boring" London, no magic, no spark, no nothing.<br><br>Each world is sealed though a special being(an Antari (ultra-rare, ultra-powerful magician) can travel between (like Kell, from Red London).<br><br>Years ago, Black London<b> fell to the mad magic </b>and was completely sealed - also sealing the fate of all those who lived there.<br><br><b>Four months ago</b>, after a series of circumstances, a black stone from Black London made its way to Red London, infecting and spreading the corrosive magic. <br><br>It was thrown back into Black London, along with Holland (the Antari from White London).<br><br>Delilah Bard, a Grey Londoner, managed to<b> finagle her way into Red London,</b> help save the day and worm her way into Kell's heart.<blockquote>
  <i>“Oh yes, your relationship with Miss Bard is positively ordinary."<br>"Be quiet."<br>"Crossing worlds, killing royals, saving cities. The marks of every good courtship.”</i>
</blockquote>But, instead of settling down, Lila Bard decided to <b>sail off and become a pirate </b>(yes, really).<blockquote>
  <i>“I know where you sleep, Bard." <br>She smirked. "Then you know I sleep with knives.” </i>
</blockquote>Now that Kell has been expressly forbidden from any unnecessary travel between Londons and Lilah is who-knows-where - for the first time, <b>Red London looks grey to him</b>.<br><br>Rhy, Kell's brother-in-name and prince of the land, decides to take over the Element Games (international magic competition) and smuggle Kell into it to<b> help him blow off steam.</b><blockquote>
  <i>Everyone thinks I have a death wish, you know? But I don't want to die - dying is easy. No, I want to live, but getting close to death is the only way to feel alive. </i>
</blockquote>But what once began as a fun, innocuous romp is <b>quickly twisting</b> out of their control. Soon, the brothers learn that Black magic never dies...<blockquote>
  <i>Everyone’s immortal until they’re not.</i>
</blockquote>This book was so much fun!<br><br>It truly felt more like<b> a companion book than an actual continuation</b> of the series and I did not mind a bit. <br><br>(Companion - because of the random tournament taking up a majority of the page space.)<br><br>It was so much fun to read about the <b>weird, whimsical world</b> of Red London - the different countries and cultures were vibrant and extremely well-done.<br><br>I found myself<b> not enjoying Delilah's character </b>as much as I did in round one. <br><br>Book one she was bada** and one tough cookie...but it felt like this round she just took everything over.<br><br>It felt like the book was more<b> focused on fulfilling Lilah's every whim </b>rather than a realistic progression of the plot and development of the characters.<br><br>Also, anyone else starting to get annoyed with the Holland thing? The rest of the characters have almost<b> a ridiculously over-the-top hatred </b>of him.<br><br>It's like, they know Holland's every move was commanded by the White London's rulers and he was tortured continuously for years...and yet they're all like, "mmm...Holland, you are a garbage human."<br><br><b>Doesn't make sense to me.</b><br><br>All in all, I did enjoy this book and I am excited for round III!<br><br><a href="http://www.mirandareads.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/miranda.reads/?hl=en" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/Miranda_Reads" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="10097532758395602100" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1923080256" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1923080256" />
    <a title="emma" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32879029-emma"><img alt="emma" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1520568130p2/32879029.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1923080256?book_show_action=true">Feb 28, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="emma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="emma" href="/user/show/32879029-emma">emma</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=unpopular-opinion">unpopular-opinion</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=nope">nope</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=diverse">diverse</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=1-star">1-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=gorgeous-covers">gorgeous-covers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=comments">comments</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1923080256" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1221185311466845080">I'd like to propose a contender for the worst feeling in the world: going into a book with 100% certainty you’ll like it, and then that confidence slowlyyyyy - almost imperceptibly - fading into hatred. Especially when the average rating of said book is a four-point-f*cking-three-five.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1488406486ra/22111181.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://emmareadstoomuch.wordpress.com/2017/03/26/a-gathering-of-shadows-review/'>https://emmareadstoomuch.wordpress.co...</a><br/><br/>But I can’t not hate this book. So much of this is nightmare scenario after nightmare scenario wrapped into one misleading synopsis. I was, quite frankly, SHOCKED by how quic</span>
  <span id="freeText1221185311466845080" style="display:none">I'd like to propose a contender for the worst feeling in the world: going into a book with 100% certainty you’ll like it, and then that confidence slowlyyyyy - almost imperceptibly - fading into hatred. Especially when the average rating of said book is a four-point-f*cking-three-five.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1488406486ra/22111181.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://emmareadstoomuch.wordpress.com/2017/03/26/a-gathering-of-shadows-review/">https://emmareadstoomuch.wordpress.co...</a><br><br>But I can’t not hate this book. So much of this is nightmare scenario after nightmare scenario wrapped into one misleading synopsis. I was, quite frankly, SHOCKED by how quickly universally adored author V.E. Schwab introduced the not-like-other-girls trope, which you all know I abhor. At least buy a girl dinner first, Victoria. I'll set the scene: Liiiiilaaaaa (read that in a sarcastically loving voice, please) is at a market. Literally looking at knives because she has no personality traits or sense of fun. Anyway, <s>another stereotype on two legs</s> the captain of her ship says, for no goddamn reason except, I presume, his own terribleness: <i>“Most girls covet dresses.”</i> Bad enough, right? Already enough to make me cringe hard and dock at least a star or so? IT GETS WORSE. Darling Lila’s response: <i>“I am not most girls.”</i> It literally cannot get any more blatant. I was so disgusted I read the scene aloud to my sister, and she <b>shuddered.</b><br><br>In fact, it’s kind of...strange how sexist this book is. The great thing about YA books is that a lot of them are written by feminists, but the subliminal messages here made my skin crawl. There’s not just the not-like-other-girls stuff (or, as I call it, Sexism Lite: So Quirky Ladies Who Hate Other Women Can Still Claim to be Feminist). Every. Single. Female character is judged for her appearance. Strong women are stripped of their gender identity - a couple of times, characters question whether muscular women are truly women at all. Which, like, f*ck you forever. Are you kidding me? And don’t forget the princess (from Vesk?). Her only character trait is boy-crazy. Instead of being a powerful female leader, she follows Kell around like a lovesick puppy...exactly, we are told, what she did to Rhy a couple years before. And don't forget the disapproving tone of the text when she's with any man. Subliminal slut shaming - cool! Oooh, and <i>“She looked like the kind of girl who would point to something — or some</i>one <i>— and say, ‘I want one of those.’”</i> Wow! Please tell me more about how there are <i>kinds</i> of girls.<br><br>More fun stuff: I literally hate all of these characters. How often does that happen?! Like, don’t get me wrong, I am completely just a heartless vessel designed to carry as much bitterness and anger as possible, but usually I’m at least <i>neutral toward somebody.</i> Not here. We follow four-ish main characters: Alucard, Rhy, Kell and Lila. (Putting Lila last because, if you couldn’t already tell by the fury leaking through this, she is the crown jewel in my treasure trove of loathing.)<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1442947740ra/16297155.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The fun thing about this book is we get two - yes, two! - characters fighting for dominance over the same piece of sh*t stereotype! Yeah, Schwab had so much success with one character in that dumbass role that she went two for two in this one. I’m talking about Rhy and Alucard, and I’m talking about the YA male character archetype that I CANNOT ESCAPE. The roguish, flirty, handsome societal elite, who’s just soooooo tired of his hard-knock life of wealth and luxury and because of it can’t even <i>stand</i> to live up to expectations or within social bounds. Also, we’re always supposed to find these types funny, and I have never cracked a smile at one of these dumbos.<br><br>I feel like I can’t goddamn escape these goons of late. They’re the Will Herondales, the what’s-his-name from Heartless (the jester guy who wore eyeliner), Adrian from Bloodlines (will I ever finish that series?), one or more of the 8000 guys from Throne of Glass (literally can’t remember). Sorry I spaced on some of the names, but there’s an epidemic of these bozos and they’re SO unmemorable. But to have TWO of the same stereotype?! In the same book?! Extraordinary. I’ve never seen anything like it (and pray I never will again).<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1488406486ra/22111184.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Now...Kell. There is no way on God’s great green Earth I can fill a paragraph talking about Kell. He is the most boring character to ever boring up his way through a trilogy. Does the boy have any traits? Does he have a sense of humor? Fun, maybe? No? He’s just going to grumble around for 500 pages and be in love with Lila for no reason? Okay.<br><br>And...here we go. The moment I’ve been waiting for since approximately page 17 of this book. Talking about why LILA SUCKS UP A STORM. The gal’s a prime example of a really annoying factor of bad character-writing: telling and not showing. How many times are we TOLD, “Lila is smart. Lila is a quick study. Lila was born with the magical talent of the Chosen One, but maybe if we don’t use that term then you won’t notice and write about it in your reviews. Lila is brave. Lila is strong. Lila looks for trouble.” Now, compare that to how often it’s actually <i>proven.</i> Rarely, if ever. It’s annoying and boring and makes me want to sign V.E. Schwab up for an intro to creative writing class.<br><br>But that’s not where my problems end with ol’ Lila. No, it takes a bit more than that to end up on my most-hated characters list. Lila’s an annoying, bossy brat with a death wish, an inferiority complex, and the impenetrable belief that she knows better than everyone else. She knows better than her captain: when she is so insubordinate that Alucard has to remind her <i>“I am your captain! You are my crew,”</i> she thinks, <i>“The barb struck with unexpected force.”</i> NOT A BARB, LILA. YOU ARE NOT IN CHARGE. YOU ARE A PETTY THIEF ABOARD A SHIP. GET OVER YOURSELF!<br><br>She does the same to the head-magicky-guy (I kind of never paid attention to the terms in this book). At one point in the last book, I guess, he told her he thought she had magic within her. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1453658323ra/17855838.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Lila latches onto that and uses it as her justification for making a metric sh*t ton of bad decisions that could have extraordinarily negative impacts on her, her loved ones, and the entire goddamn world(s). When Chief Inspector Magic tries to prevent her from making one of these many dumb choices, she responds, <i>"You told me that I had magic in me. Now you don't think I have what it takes?"</i> Um, you’re untrained and a full-on dumbass and you want this guy who actually knows his stuff to fan your already-enormous ego and tell you you can win a huge magic tournament?<br><br>And she does it again, to Kell, who knows more about her and more about the kind of magic she wants to do than ANYONE. And she’s just a total bitch to him and he’s all, “yeah ok” and kisses her stupid face. Ugh. I’m getting so angry AND putting off math homework that’s due in 37 minutes. It’s time to stop talking about Lila and try to wrap this shindig up.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1488406486ra/22111187.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>So much of this book is just...cliche to me. That moment when Lila is talking to the man at the mirror stall and he calls her Lila and she goes, all quasi-spook-ily, <i>It wasn't until after I left that I realized I had never told him my name....................</i> or whatever? Made me GAG. And it wasn't even <i>for</i> anything! That guy never comes back. We never get more info, really, on the mirrors or on the shopkeeper or any of that. It's just a dumb cliche being used for a dumb cliched manner of foreshadowing. Like, omg, does she <i>want</i> the dark power slash thing she is entirely uneducated about?! Even though she shouldn't?? Even though the big strong experienced man warns her not to do whatever said thing is? Oh my god! I have never read anything like that before! Except, like, you know...The Winner's Kiss, Divergent, Siege and Storm, Throne of Glass, The 5th Wave, Passenger, Rebel Belle, Alice. I could definitely go on. Because that is one of my least favorite tropes that also manages to be super boring in every instance it is used. Seriously, shall I ever cease to be astounded by the untouched realms of young adult fantasy this book doth discover?<br><br>And after all that, it’s not even fun. I wanted to read about a magic tournament, but it took 350 pages to get there and only lasted about 100 (generously). The rest of the book is a carbon copy of the events of the last book. I don’t want to spoil anything, but the grand cliffhanger of the book happens in the exact same way at the exact same event as the last book. It is, in other words, a snoozefest.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1488406486ra/22111188.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Bottom line: clichéd, sexist, teeming with some of the worst characters I’ve ever read, misleading, repetitive, occasionally illogical, and boring. Does that sum it up? Bleh.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1221185311466845080" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1451716703" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1451716703" />
    <a title="Hannah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/38077205-hannah"><img alt="Hannah" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1569937560p2/38077205.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

<span id="freeTextContainer15660367655497975943"><i>The prince shrugged. “Who needs magic when you look this good?”</i><br/><br/>This book set fire to my feelings and shattered my mind. Tore my heart into pieces and stole my soul.<br/>I am officially and utterly dead.<br/><br/>Victoria Schwab worked her magic like a genius. This book was flawless, from start to finish. From cover to characters, from plot to setting, from language to imagination. And while I thought <i>A Darker Shade of Magic</i> was amazing, it was only the tip of the iceberg. Nothing can compare to <i>A Gathering of </i></span>
  <span id="freeText15660367655497975943" style="display:none"><i>The prince shrugged. “Who needs magic when you look this good?”</i><br /><br />This book set fire to my feelings and shattered my mind. Tore my heart into pieces and stole my soul.<br />I am officially and utterly dead.<br /><br />Victoria Schwab worked her magic like a genius. This book was flawless, from start to finish. From cover to characters, from plot to setting, from language to imagination. And while I thought <i>A Darker Shade of Magic</i> was amazing, it was only the tip of the iceberg. Nothing can compare to <i>A Gathering of Shadows</i>. (...well. Harry Potter can. But, I mean, please...)<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Now let me talk freely. Lila is a unique character but Saints she annoyed me in the end. Stubborn to a point of being stupid! But oh I am so glad for Alucards existence, or better for that HEAVENLY KISS SCENE OH MY GOD. Please, Victoria, let them share lots of private moments and make-out scenes in ADSOM #3!!! I've never been much of a shipper but these two give me everything. Rhy is one of my favourite ever characters and even if everything goes to ruins, as long as Rhy and Alucard are together in the end, I will be satisfied.<br />But no, really, I don't know where this is going. Lila will probably save Kell, I guess. And I won't be surprised if one or more important characters end up dead. But that's as far as it goes with my guessing. What is happening to Rhy? To Kell? Red London? Grey and White London? Alucard? The King and the Queen(fuck them tho.) The other Kingdoms? I have no idea. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />The ending was - minor spoiler here - a stab in the chest. A Cliffhanger. Meaning endless waiting time for the sequel. How will I survive this?<br /><br /> <a href="https://www.instagram.com/fantasticbooksandwheretofindem/" rel="nofollow noopener">Find more of my books on Instagram</a></span>

    <a title="Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10336538-jessica-silverbow"><img alt="Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1393785730p2/10336538.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1218954728?book_show_action=true">Mar 05, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ " href="/user/show/10336538-jessica-silverbow">Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=rabid-reads-reviews">rabid-reads-reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=pirates">pirates</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=some-kinda-magic">some-kinda-magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=the-book-boy-is-mine">the-book-boy-is-mine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=shiny">shiny</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=from-publisher">from-publisher</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=kickass-heroines">kickass-heroines</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=it-burns-us-precious">it-burns-us-precious</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=cover-whore">cover-whore</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1218954728" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11144153013560917950"><b>Reviewed by: <a href='http://rabidreads.ca/2016/02/early-review-a-gathering-of-shadows-by-v-e-schwab-jessicadhaluska-veschwab-torteen-torbooks.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>Rabid Reads</a></b><br/><br/><b>4.5 stars</b><br/><br/>Authors of series like to do this thing where they give you a first installment that while, <i>of course</i>, leaving unanswered questions, still manages to conclude nice and neatly.<br/><br/>You can't wait to get your hands on the next book, but only b/c you love the story and are desperate to see what happens next. <br/><br/>You feel safe when you finally get the next chapter. <br/><br/>The tension that plagued you while reading the prior installment, coming ever closer as you neared the end, like</span>
  <span id="freeText11144153013560917950" style="display:none"><b>Reviewed by: <a href="http://rabidreads.ca/2016/02/early-review-a-gathering-of-shadows-by-v-e-schwab-jessicadhaluska-veschwab-torteen-torbooks.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Rabid Reads</a></b><br><br><b>4.5 stars</b><br><br>Authors of series like to do this thing where they give you a first installment that while, <i>of course</i>, leaving unanswered questions, still manages to conclude nice and neatly.<br><br>You can't wait to get your hands on the next book, but only b/c you love the story and are desperate to see what happens next. <br><br>You feel safe when you finally get the next chapter. <br><br>The tension that plagued you while reading the prior installment, coming ever closer as you neared the end, like footsteps speeding up behind you, making you curse your stupidity for taking a walk alone at night in an unfamiliar city . . . That tension isn't there.<br><br>You've developed a trust, a camaraderie . . . an <i>understanding</i> with the author.<br><br>
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1453842344ra/17880035.gif" width="500" height="500" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
<br><br>You have been duly warned.<br><br>When we last left Lila and Kell, they were parting ways. We were sad, but we expected no less. After all:<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“I’m not going to die,” she said. “Not till I’ve seen it.”<br>“Seen what?”<br>Her smile widened. “Everything.”</i>
</blockquote><br>Kell can't go with her. He has responsibilities . . . PLUS, you know, there's <i>that thing</i> that happened, <i>that thing</i> that tied him even closer to the royal family . . . The royal family he's meant to be part of . . . The royal family that instead treats him like a commodity . . . <br><br>Lemme tell you, people--it gets WORSE.<br><br>Lila, on the other hand, is having the adventure she's always dreamed of. On a PIRATE ship. *coughs* I mean, privateer ship. She got her position by killing another crew member. *shakes head at Lila* Buuuuut it turned out they didn't like the fellow much anyway, so it all worked out. <br><br>A little <i>too</i> well, actually. <br><br>Lila develops a sort-of friendship with the captain. She earns the respect of the crew. <i>Worse</i>, she begins to feel like she herself is a true part of the crew.<br><br>Can't have that. <br><br>So when Captain announces his intent to return to Red London and participate in a prestigious wizards' tournament, Lila decides that she won't be going with them when next they leave.<br><br>And she doesn't. <br><br>But not for the reasons she anticipated. <br><br><b>You:</b> WHAT DOES THAT MEAN?!<br><br><b>Me:</b> 
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1453842344ra/17880035.gif" width="500" height="500" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
<br><br>And that's just the tip of the iceberg. <br><br>Things happen in A DARKER SHADE OF MAGIC, and those things have CONSEQUENCES. CONSEQUENCES that you will not believe until you see them for yourself. <br><br>What does it mean that Kell's life is now tied to another's? What will happen now that a living being from Grey London has permanently crossed over into Red London? And what would you say if I told you that you only <i>think</i> you've seen chaos in White London?<br><br>Last year, A DARKER SHADE OF MAGIC made my Best Books of 2015 list. This year, A GATHERING OF SHADOWS is already a strong contender for the #1 spot. If you have yet to check out Schwab for yourself, what are you waiting for? The woman is GENIUS. This world and the characters that populate it are one of the most unique I've encountered in ages. I love it. Even as I'm screaming at Lila to THINK before she acts. For once. Even as my heart is breaking for Kell, b/c he can longer ignore the charade of his circumstances. Even as all the Londons hover on the edge of DOOM . . . I love it. <br><br>Highly recommended.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1421060968i/13316940.jpg" alt="Jessica Signature" width="205" height="101" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>My other reviews for this series:</b><br><br><b>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/941896221" rel="nofollow noopener">A Darker Shade of Magic (Shades of Magic, #1)</a>
</b><br><b>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1510375081" rel="nofollow noopener">A Conjuring of Light (Shades of Magic, #3)</a>
</b></span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781250222060" href="/book/show/41085124-a-gathering-of-shadows">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=owned-audio">owned-audio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=audio">audio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=diverse-reads">diverse-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=owned-physical">owned-physical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=otp">otp</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=lgbtqiap">lgbtqiap</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=the-best-of-the-best">the-best-of-the-best</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1971365618" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4440713654248335156"><blockquote>#1 <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1920506835' rel='nofollow noopener'>A Darker Shade of Magic</a> ★★★★★ <br/>#2 <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1971365618' rel='nofollow noopener'>A Gathering of Shadows</a> ★★★★★<br/>#3 <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2122460535' rel='nofollow noopener'>A Conjuring of Light</a> ★★★★★</blockquote> <br/>I cannot believe that I waited nearly a <i>year</i> between the first book and this one, but here we are, and now I’m convinced that Victoria sacrificed an unhealthy number of virgins for her writing skills, because this series is absolute magnificence. I loved <i>A Darker Shade of Magic</i> so much that I was nervous to see if the second book would hold up, but let me tell you, it absolutely did, and now I am both h</span>
  <span id="freeText4440713654248335156" style="display:none"><blockquote>#1 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1920506835" rel="nofollow noopener">A Darker Shade of Magic</a> ★★★★★ <br />#2 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1971365618" rel="nofollow noopener">A Gathering of Shadows</a> ★★★★★<br />#3 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2122460535" rel="nofollow noopener">A Conjuring of Light</a> ★★★★★</blockquote> <br />I cannot believe that I waited nearly a <i>year</i> between the first book and this one, but here we are, and now I’m convinced that Victoria sacrificed an unhealthy number of virgins for her writing skills, because this series is absolute magnificence. I loved <i>A Darker Shade of Magic</i> so much that I was nervous to see if the second book would hold up, but let me tell you, it absolutely did, and now I am both horrified and desperately in need of seeing how it all ends up.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i> “I am Delilah Bard,” she thought, as the ropes cut into her skin. “I am a thief and a pirate and a traveler. I have set foot in three different worlds, and lived. I have shed the blood of royals and held magic in my hands.”</i>
</blockquote><br />I only thought that I loved the characters of this series in the first book, but that was nothing compared to the feelings that I have for them by this point. There’s Lila, who took me a little bit of time to be won over by in <i>ADSOM,</i> but who has me utterly captivated in this installment. Her brash, headstrong, clever nature is only magnified even further as she comes into her own in the world of Red London, and while she still feels this evident need to prove herself and to come out on top, her entire attitude has been tempered—if only slightly—by the pains that her previous actions have caused. She’s also still determined to avoid dealing with her feelings towards a certain redheaded Antari, which lends beautifully to the <i>incredible</i> slow burn of the brief romantic undertones to these books.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i> “I do not know why you two are circling each other like stars. It is not my cosmic dance. But I do know that you come asking after one another, when only a few strides and a handful of stars divide you.”</i>
</blockquote><br />Precious Kell, on the other hand, is still my favorite; I’m constantly torn between being amazed by his skills and abilities, and wanting to jump in and protect him from the cruelty he faces, not only as one of the last remaining Antari, but as the neglected adopted son of the King and Queen. My years of reading fantasy novels have taught me that it’s difficult for me to relate to “lawful good” characters who rely so heavily on their virtues and honor, as Kell does, but Victoria writes him so flawlessly that it never grows stale or predictable. On top of everything else, his relationship with his brother, Rhy, is one of the most wholesome, pure, and <i>precious</i> things I have ever seen in my entire life.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>Rhy held Kell’s pain in his hands, while Kell held Rhy’s life in his.</i>
</blockquote><br />Rhy Maresh is, I think, one of the most lovable fictional characters who has ever been written. I don’t know if I have ever met a fan of this series who does not adore him at least a little bit, especially upon getting to know the quiet self-loathing that resides under his charisma and charm. He broke my heart so many times during his struggles with the lengths Kell has gone to in order to save him, and the fact that he values his own presence in the world so little is crushing, yet nevertheless, Rhy is a constant source of drama, amusement, and sweet brotherly love in a world full of violence and fear. The fact that both of these princes would so readily give up everything for one another is perhaps my single favorite aspect to this gorgeous series thus far.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i> “Fix your crown, my prince,” he called back as he reached the door. “It’s crooked.”</i>
</blockquote><br />Of course, this review would be wholly incomplete without taking a moment to talk about the utterly fantastic addition to the cast: Alucard Emery, privateer, playboy, magical aficionado, and captain of the Night Spire crew. He is hilarious, delightful in every way, and an absolute deviant who never fails to keep you guessing. I love his entire presence in the story, and though I am left with a million and one questions about his past and how it relates to the lives of the Maresh family, it is easily one of the things that I am <i>most</i> excited about tying up in <i>A Conjuring of Light.</i><br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i> “Magic is tangled, so you must be smooth.<br />Magic is wild, so you must be tame.<br />Magic is chaos, so you must be calm.<br />Are you calm, Kell?”</i>
</blockquote><br />Besides the wonderful cast of characters (including one special individual who I’m not going to mention here for fear of spoiling anyone, but let me say that I am absolutely ecstatic to see things through his perspective on occasion, and terrified to see what he will do next), there’s also the fact that, once again, Victoria proves her writing prowess through incredible action scenes and magical world-building. There is a tournament featured in this installment that never grows stale or dull; despite its potential for repetition, as is frequent with “trials” in books, not once did I lose the feeling of gripping the edge of my seat.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i> “I gave him my life, but you cannot ask me to stop living.”</i>
</blockquote><br />This sequel also delves much further into the history of Red London and its surrounding lands, as well as the political climate between the kingdom of Arnes and its allies and potential enemies. It was such a fantastic buildup of information, but I can’t help but wonder how it can all possibly be addressed in the finale. That said, I have no doubts that I will be pleased with how everything turns out (and it doesn’t hurt that I know there are further books coming along in the future, too!).<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>They crashed into each other as if propelled by gravity, and he didn’t know which one of them was the object and which the earth, only that they were colliding.</i>
</blockquote><br />I don’t think I can say too much more without spoiling any of the twists and turns in this installment, so I’ll end this review on this note: if you enjoy fantasy worlds with lovable characters, a brilliant (yet never overdone) magic system, world-building and history for days, and enough twists and turns to never let you find a moment’s rest, I cannot recommend this series highly enough—and I cannot wait to read the final piece to the story!<br /><br />---<br /><br />Buddy read with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/51076954-terry-tipton" rel="nofollow noopener">Terry</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/7772979-jue" rel="nofollow noopener">Julie</a>! ♥♥♥<br /><br />You can find this review and more on my <a href="https://howlinglibraries.com/2018/05/23/a-gathering-of-shadows/" rel="nofollow noopener">blog</a>, or you can follow me on <a href="https://twitter.com/howlinglibrary" rel="nofollow noopener">twitter</a>, <a href="https://instagram.com/howlinglibraries" rel="nofollow noopener">bookstagram</a>, or <a href="https://facebook.com/howlinglibraries" rel="nofollow noopener">facebook</a>!</span>
  <a data-text-id="4440713654248335156" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer5400729329588406615">okay. i knew this was going to be good, but i didnt expect it to be <i>that</i> good. oh sanct, that ending. im giving this five stars for the last 100 pages alone - my heart is RACING. and im beyond happy the third book is already out because i dont know how people managed to be patient enough to wait. <br/><br/>so where i thought the first book excelled in its world building by introducing the four different londons and their histories, i found the sequel gave amazing insight into the characters, more of their</span>
  <span id="freeText5400729329588406615" style="display:none">okay. i knew this was going to be good, but i didnt expect it to be <i>that</i> good. oh sanct, that ending. im giving this five stars for the last 100 pages alone - my heart is RACING. and im beyond happy the third book is already out because i dont know how people managed to be patient enough to wait. <br /><br />so where i thought the first book excelled in its world building by introducing the four different londons and their histories, i found the sequel gave amazing insight into the characters, more of their development was prevalent, and it even introduced some new key people. both aspects are important, but together they make one heck of a story. what really impressed me was how this didnt feel like a filler book, which many second books tend to be. but rather, this felt like a seamless, yet crucial, part of bridge that connects all three books. <br /><br />again, this was a little bit of a slow burner, but it was much easier for me to get into because i felt like there was a little more going on. i really wish the games had taken up much more of the book - i found them so interesting - but i cant complain because the last 25% or so gave the reader so much. and the writing was on point, as always. <br /><br />there is no question in my mind as to why this series is as loved as it is, so let the binge reading continue!<br /><br /><b>↠ <i>4.5 stars</i></b></span>

<div id="review_1712921573" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781250222060" href="/book/show/41085124-a-gathering-of-shadows">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17438949-melissa-dog-wolf-lover-martin?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17438949-melissa-dog-wolf-lover-martin?shelf=fantasy-all">fantasy-all</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17438949-melissa-dog-wolf-lover-martin?shelf=own">own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1712921573" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12276138612637930021"><b>LOOK</b><br/><br/><img src='https://s3.amazonaws.com/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1552664132r/27210312.jpg?v=1552664135420' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><img src='https://s3.amazonaws.com/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1552664092r/27210311.jpg?v=1552664095579' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><img src='https://s3.amazonaws.com/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1552664175r/27210313.jpg?v=1552664178406' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1470533434ra/19938690.gif' alt=' ' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1470533434ra/19938691.gif' alt=' ' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I got to read more of the bad arsed, Lila Bard and Kell and Rhy! Yay! <br/><br/>I loved the beginning of this book with Lila. People for me, this was the best part of the book with what all Lila did to that crew! Holy crow! <br/><br/><b>I am Delilah Bard, she though as the ropes cut into her skin. I am a thief and a pirate and a traveler. I have set foot in three different worlds, and lived. I have shed the blood of royals and held magic in my hands. And a ship full of men cannot do what I can, I don't need any of</b></span>
  <span id="freeText12276138612637930021" style="display:none"><b>LOOK</b><br><br><img src="https://s3.amazonaws.com/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1552664132r/27210312.jpg?v=1552664135420" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://s3.amazonaws.com/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1552664092r/27210311.jpg?v=1552664095579" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://s3.amazonaws.com/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1552664175r/27210313.jpg?v=1552664178406" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1470533434ra/19938690.gif" alt=" " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1470533434ra/19938691.gif" alt=" " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I got to read more of the bad arsed, Lila Bard and Kell and Rhy! Yay! <br><br>I loved the beginning of this book with Lila. People for me, this was the best part of the book with what all Lila did to that crew! Holy crow! <br><br><b>I am Delilah Bard, she though as the ropes cut into her skin. I am a thief and a pirate and a traveler. I have set foot in three different worlds, and lived. I have shed the blood of royals and held magic in my hands. And a ship full of men cannot do what I can, I don't need any of you. I am one of a damned kind.</b><br><br>I also fell in love with Lila's captain aboard the Night Spire - Captain Aluccard Emery. He's so awesome! He is a little bit of this and a little bit of that and a whole lot of coolness =)<br><br>Not a whole lot goes on in the book after the fun stuff in the beginning. I feel it's just another set up for more things to come in the next book. <br><br>At some point though, magic welders come together in The Element Games called <b>Essen Tasch</b>. Some people I didn't expect were in these games and against each other. It was pretty damn cool! <br><br>I loved reading about Kell and Rhy together again. They are so funny and caring. They are so close in everything they do and it was so wonderful to see them fighting for each other. To read the things that only love for someone you consider your brother can bring to your heart. Rhy wants Kell to compete in the games but Kell doesn't want to for certain reasons. <br><br><b>"Kell. My greatest fear in life isn't dying. It's being the source of someone else's suffering. I know you feel trapped. I know I'm your cage. And I can't---" His voice broke, and Kell could feel his brother's pain, everything he tried to smother until dark and drown until morning. "You will do this, " said Rhy. "For me. For both of us." <br>Kell held his brother's gaze. "All right,"he said.</b><br><br>And Lila and Kell get to see each other again. And Rhy too, the whole gang. It was so great! And then . . . that ending!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1470533694ra/19938700.gif" alt=" " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Something Wicked This Way Comes</b><br><br>MY BLOG: <a href="http://melissa413readsalot.blogspot.com/2016/08/a-gathering-of-shadows-by-ve-schwab.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Melissa Martin's Reading List</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="12276138612637930021" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1891188052" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1891188052" />
    <a title="Elle (ellexamines)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/52545435-elle-ellexamines"><img alt="Elle (ellexamines)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582250895p2/52545435.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1891188052?book_show_action=true">Feb 15, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elle (ellexamines)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elle (ellexamines)" href="/user/show/52545435-elle-ellexamines">Elle (ellexamines)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Everyone</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=z-read2017">z-read2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=sff-high-fantasy">sff-high-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=genre-experiments">genre-experiments</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=x-series">x-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=z-faves2017">z-faves2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=5-star">5-star</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1891188052" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11827040938027830511"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“You tried to seduce me, for information.”<br/>“You can’t hold that against me forever.”<br/>“It was last night.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/><b>PART ONE: CHARACTERIZATION</b><br/><i>Alternate Title: mecrying.mp3</i><br/><br/>Kell is such an infinitely relatable bitter asshole of a character. He's a bit morally imperfect and he's so infinitely lovable. <br/><br/>Lila is completely bitter and can be reckless, but she's such a consistent character and I genuinely love her so. so. much. <a href='https://bookriot.com/2016/05/04/lila-bard-hero-shades-magic-series/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Please read this essay talking about Lila Bard and narrative agency it's smar</a></span>
  <span id="freeText11827040938027830511" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“You tried to seduce me, for information.”<br />“You can’t hold that against me forever.”<br />“It was last night.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br /><b>PART ONE: CHARACTERIZATION</b><br /><i>Alternate Title: mecrying.mp3</i><br /><br />Kell is such an infinitely relatable bitter asshole of a character. He's a bit morally imperfect and he's so infinitely lovable. <br /><br />Lila is completely bitter and can be reckless, but she's such a consistent character and I genuinely love her so. so. much. <a href="https://bookriot.com/2016/05/04/lila-bard-hero-shades-magic-series/" rel="nofollow noopener">Please read this essay talking about Lila Bard and narrative agency it's smart and I'm exhausted</a><br /><br />Rhy's character development is so awesome. In the first book, he was an okay character, but in this second book I loved him with every fiber of my heart. He's got some hidden depths and he's so interesting and funny. <br /><br />The side characters killed me too, of course. Alucard is funny and a ton of fun. Holland is so morally bankrupt and yet I love him so, so much. <br /><br />God, I love every character in this book so much. Someone please punch me in the face. <br /><br /><b>PART TWO: RELATIONSHIPS</b><br /><i>Alternate Title: mecryingharder.mp3</i><br /><br />There's kind of a love square going on here, and it makes the book even better. I know that sentence sounds contradictory. But trust me, there's no annoying love triangle here. There are complex dynamics between characters, but it's not for drama. <br /><br />V.E. Schwab does an incredible job with the platonic relationships here. I especially loved Lila and Alucard's banter. <br /><br />The romance is built up very subtly and not the major focus. But oh damn, is it well written. Lila and Kell are a very well-built couple, and V.E. Schwab drew out the plot enough that I was begging for them to interact. That's talent. <br /><br />Please just let them be happy. I just want all of them to be happy. Damn it. <br /><br /><b>PART THREE: PLOTTING AND WRITING</b><br /><i>Alternate Title: meSCREAMING.mp3</i><br /><br />V.E. Schwab's writing is gorgeous as always. Her talent for describing setting especially stands out here. Usually I can't picture any settings in books, but I have such clear mental images of every moment of this book. And it never feels forced at all! <br /><br />The plot is twisty and interesting. Saying anything about it is a spoiler, but I had so many emotions here. To be fair, I guessed one of the major twists, but I had been spoiled about an aspect of it, so that's not the books' fault at all. <br /><br />However, the lack of direction to the plot in the first half bothered me. On one hand, I loved the extended character work and worldbuilding in the first half. On the other hand, none of the characters had any clear goal until around page 250, and the plot felt slightly less driven as a result. This is a complaint I had about book one as well. <br /><br />All in all, I absolutely loved this. I worship Schwab to such a high degree. She's so talented.<br />div17: pansexual mc</span>
  <a data-text-id="11827040938027830511" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
